the accrual method of accounting.</font>

computed based on the weighted average number of shares actually outstanding. 
&nbsp;&nbsp;Diluted net income (loss) per share amounts are computed using the 
weighted average number of common and common equivalent shares outstanding as if
shares had been issued on the exercise of the common share rights unless the 
exercise becomes antid</font><font style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-

are&nbsp;</font><font style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-

style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',Times,serif;">As 
of&nbsp;</font><font style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">April 30</font><font style="font-

were 30,000,000 (from convertible debt) and 0 potential common 
shares</font><font style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">.</font>

for impairment when events or changes in circumstances indicate that the related
carrying amounts may not be recoverable. &nbsp;The assets are subject to 
impairment consideration under ASC 360-10-35-17 if events or circumstances 
indicate that their carrying amounts might not be recoverable. When the Company 
determines that an impairment analysis should be done, the analysis will be 
performed using rules of ASC 930-360-35, Asset Impairment, and 360-10-15-3 
through 15-5, Impairment or Disposal of Long-Lived Assets.</font>

</div>
<div style="text-align:justify;background-color:;text-
indent:0px;padding-left:48px;padding-right:0px; margin-top:8px;margin-
bottom:0px;border-width:1px 1px 1px 1px; border-style:none none none none;style-
template-id:0;">
&nbsp;

<div style="text-align:justify;background-color:;text-
indent:0px;padding-left:48px;padding-right:0px; margin-top:8px;margin-
bottom:0px;border-width:1px 1px 1px 1px; border-style:none none none none;style-
template-id:0;"><font style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">Investments in companies that are not consolidated,
but over which the Company exercises significant influence, are accounted for 
under the equity method of accounting. Whether or not the Company exercises 
significant influence with respect to an investee depends on an evaluation of 
several factors, including, among others, ownership level. Under the equity 
method of accounting, an investee company&#8217;s accounts are not reflected 
within the Company&#8217;s Balance Sheets and Statements of Operations; however,
the Company&#8217;s share of the earnings or losses of the investee company is 
reflected in the Company&#8217;s Statements of Operations and the 
Company&#8217;s carrying value in an equity method investee company is reflected
in the Company&#8217;s Balance Sheets. The Company evaluates these investments 
for other-than-temporary declines in value each quarterly period. Any impairment
found to be other than temporary would be recorded through a charge to earnings.
As of&nbsp;</font><font style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">April 30</font><font style="font-
size:15px;color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',Times,serif;">, 2014</font><font 
style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',Times,serif;">&nbsp;and 
2013,</font><font style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">&nbsp;the Company recorded impairment losses on the
New World investment of $</font><font style="font-size:15px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">272,990</font><font style="font-
size:15px;color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',Times,serif;">&nbsp;and $0, 
respectively.</font>

</div>
<div style="text-align:justify;background-color:;text-

<div style="text-align:justify;background-color:;text-
indent:0px;padding-left:0px;padding-right:0px; margin-top:8px;margin-
bottom:0px;border-width:1px 1px 1px 1px; border-style:none none none none;style-
template-id:0;"><font style="font-size:13px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">The transfer of concessions in Mexico must be 
registered under Mexican law.&nbsp;&nbsp;We have been advised that the transfer 
of the concessions to New World Metals has been registered with the appropriate 
Mexican authorities.</font><font style="font-size:13px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;"><b>&nbsp;</b></font><font style="font-
size:13px;color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',Times,serif;">Under Mexican law, a 
mining concession gives the holder both exploration and exploitation rights for 
any minerals found in the property.&nbsp;&nbsp;To maintain the concession, the 
holder must pay appropriate taxes, perform assessment work, comply with 
environmental laws, and file a production report each year with the appropriate 
authorities.&nbsp;&nbsp;Foreign individuals and companies wanting to hold 
concessions must do so through ownership in a Mexican corporation or through a 
joint venture and they may not hold mining concessions 
directly.&nbsp;&nbsp;Because of those requirements, we rely on New World Metals,
persons associated with New World Metals, and its employees and consultants in 
Mexico, to perform all acts necessary to comply with the legal requirements 
necessary to maintain the concessions.</font>

template-id:0;"><font style="font-size:13px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">The mineralization is believed to be a low 
sulphadation epithermal deposit in quartz and calcite vein structures. The gold 
and silver on the properties is found in these veins and the host rock is 
shale.</font>
</div>
<div style="text-align:justify;background-color:;text-
indent:0px;padding-left:26px;padding-right:0px; margin-top:8px;margin-

template-id:0;"><font style="font-size:13px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">We hold an indirect 45% interest in this mine 
through our investment in New World. New World owns a direct interest in this 
mine. In 2013, major repairs and upgrades have been carried out to the mining 
structure at the Morelos Mine.&nbsp;Current assays at this new level show 1 gram
of Gold and 200 grams of Silver per ton.&nbsp;The Morelos mine is 21 hectares 
and has gold and silver as its main minerals with assays averaging 2 grams of 
gold and 600 grams of silver per ton. Currently there is a stockpile of 6,000 
tons of ore ready to process. Production is currently 30 tons per day.</font>

from these estimates.&nbsp;</font>

</div>
<div style="text-align:justify;background-color:;text-

template-id:0;"><font style="font-size:13px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">The Company utilizes the liability method of 
accounting for income taxes. &nbsp;Under the liability method deferred tax 
assets and liabilities are determined based on differences between financial 
reporting and the tax bases of the assets and liabilities and are measured using
the enacted tax rates and laws that will be in effect, when the differences are 
expected to be reversed. &nbsp;&nbsp;An allowance against deferred tax assets is
recorded, when it is more likely than not, that such tax benefits will not be
realized.</font>

controls and procedures that are designed to ensure that information required to

on. &nbsp;They will also have full control over matters that require Board of 
Directors approval. This may introduce conflicts of interest and prevent the 
segregation of executive duties from those that require Board of 
Directors&#8217; approval. &nbsp;This may lead to ineffective disclosure and 
accounting controls. &nbsp;None compliance with laws and regulations may result 
in fines and penalties. &nbsp;They would have the ability to take any action as 
they themselves review them and approve them. &nbsp;They would exercise control 
over all matters requiring shareholder approval including significant corporate 
transactions. &nbsp;We have not implemented various corporate governance 
measures nor have we adopted any independent committees as we presently do not
have any independent directors. &nbsp;</font>

<div style="text-align:left;background-color:;text-
indent:0px;padding-left:0px;padding-right:0px; margin-top:8px;margin-
bottom:0px;border-width:1px 1px 1px 1px; border-style:none none none none;style-
template-id:0;"><font style="font-size:13px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">Mineral deposit estimates are imprecise and subject
to error, and resource calculations when made may prove unreliable. 
&nbsp;Assumptions made regarding the supporting data may prove inaccurate and 
unforeseen events may lead to further inaccuracies. &nbsp;Sample variability, 
mining and processing adjustments, environmental changes, metal price 
fluctuations, and law and regulation changes are all factors that could lead to 
deviances from the original estimations. No assurances can be given that any 
mineral deposit estimate will ever be reclassified as a reserve. &nbsp;We have 
no known ore reserves. &nbsp;Despite future investment in exploration 
activities, there is no guarantee we will locate a commercially viable ore 
reserve. &nbsp;Most exploration projects do no result in discovery of 
commercially mineable deposits. With little capital available, we will have to 
limit our exploration which decreases the chances of finding a commercially 
viable ore body. Even if gold is identified, La Carlota may not be put into 
production due to high extraction costs, low gold prices, or inadequate amount 
and reduced recovery rates. &nbsp;If the exploration activities do not suggest a
commercially successful prospect then we may altogether abandon plans to develop
the property.</font>
</div>
<div style="text-align:left;background-color:;text-
indent:0px;padding-left:0px;padding-right:0px; margin-top:8px;margin-

is speculative and extremely competitive which may make success 
difficult.&nbsp;</i></b></font>
</div>
indent:0px;padding-left:0px;padding-right:0px; margin-top:8px;margin-

<div style="text-align:left;background-color:;text-

template-id:0;"><font style="font-size:13px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">&nbsp;We face strong competition from other mining 
companies for the acquisition of new properties. &nbsp;New properties increase 
the probability of discovering a profitable reserve. &nbsp;Most companies have 
greater financial and managerial resources than we do and can acquire and 
explore attractive new mining properties. &nbsp;We will face similar 
difficulties raising new capital to expand operations against the larger, better
capitalized competitors. Limited supply and unforeseen demand from larger, more 
competitive companies may make secure all necessary equipment and materials 
difficult and may result in periodic interruptions or even business failure. 
Success depends on a combination of many factors including but not limited to: 
the quality of management, technical (geological) expertise, quality of land 
available for exploration and the capital available for exploration.</font>

template-id:0;"><font style="font-size:13px;color:#000000;font-
family:'Arial',Times,serif;">We have placed our Mexican mineral projects into 
production without first establishing mineral reserves supported by a technical 
report and completing a feasibility study. Historically, such projects have a 
much higher risk of economic or technical failure. We have not based our 
production decision on a pre-feasibility or feasibility study of mineral 
reserves, which demonstrate our economic and technical viability. As a result, 
there is increased uncertainty, with specific economic and technical failure 
associated with this decision.</font>
</div>

price tends to be linked to a number of factors beyond our control such as: 
various macroeconomic factors (terrorism, political and regional events that may
include such, confidence in the global monetary system, rate of inflation 
expectations, interest rates, US dollar and certain other currency strength); 
speculative or hedging activities; forward sales by producers, speculators and 
other holders; central bank lending; sales and purchases of gold; industrial and
jewellery demand; and the current supply and demand. &nbsp;These things are 
impossible for us to predict. &nbsp;Per ounce, gold has been $384 (1995), $279 
(2000), $420 (2005), $1,120 (2010), $1,834 (2011)</font><font style="font-
size:13px;color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',Times,serif;">, $1,754

any sort of insurance and may have difficulties obtaining such once operations 
start as insurance is generally sparse and cost prohibitive.</font>

family:'Arial',Times,serif;">Raising additional capital through future offerings
of common stock may be necessary for our company to continue going, but there is
no guarantee that this will be possible. &nbsp;Doing so will, however, dilute 
percentage of our Company&#8217;s shares presently held by our shareholders. 
Financing may be achieved by issuing more shares which will increase the number 
of common shares outstanding. &nbsp;This will decrease the percentage interest 
held by each of our shareholders. &nbsp;As the total number of outstanding 
common shares increases, the equity attached to any individual share will 
decrease causing a dilution of shareholders&#8217; ownership over the company. 
&nbsp;With little other access to funds currently, we may have to rely on this 
method substantially to raise additional capital. &nbsp;</font>

family:'Arial',Times,serif;"><i>As our stock is a penny stock, there are 
restrictions imposed by the United States Securities and Exchange 
Commission&#8217;s (&#8220;SEC&#8221;) penny stock regulations and the 
FINRA&#8217;s sales practice requirements. &nbsp;This might limit a 
shareholder&#8217;s ability to buy and sell their shares as broker-dealers may 
be less likely to engage in transactions of our common shares. &nbsp;A penny 
stock generally includes any non-NASDAQ equity security that has a market price 
of less than $5.00 per share. &nbsp;Our common stock is expected to trade well
below that mark. &nbsp;Rules 15g-1 through 15g-9 under the Exchange Act impose 
sale practice and disclosure requirements on certain brokers-dealers who engage 
in certain transactions involving a &#8220;penny stock&#8221;</i></font>
